        </tr>

      <p><b>Namibia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Namibia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/En-ca-Namibia.oga" class="internal" title="En-ca-Namibia.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Namibia</b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>. Its western border is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>; it shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> to the south and east. Although <a href="/wiki/Kazungula" title="Kazungula">it does not</a> border <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, less than 200 metres (660 feet) of the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi" title="Zambezi">Zambezi River</a> separates the two countries. Namibia gained independence from South Africa on 21 March 1990, following the <a href="/wiki/Namibian_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Namibian War of Independence">Namibian War of Independence</a>. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a>. Namibia is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN), the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU) and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>The driest country in Sub-Saharan Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Namibia has been inhabited since early times by the <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damara_people" title="Damara people">Damara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Nama people</a>. Around the 14th century, <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrating</a> <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> arrived as part of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a>. Since then, the Bantu groups, the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo</a>, have dominated the population of the country; since the late 19th century, they have constituted a majority. </p>
      <p>In 1878, the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape of Good Hope</a>, then a British colony, annexed the port of <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> and the offshore <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Islands" title="Penguin Islands">Penguin Islands</a>; these became an integral part of the new <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> at its creation in 1910. In 1884 the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> established rule over most of the territory, forming a colony known as <a href="/wiki/German_South_West_Africa" title="German South West Africa">German South West Africa</a>. It developed farming and infrastructure. Between 1904 and 1908 it perpetrated a <a href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua genocide">genocide</a> against the Herero and Nama people. German rule ended in 1915 with a defeat by South African forces. In 1920, after the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">mandated</a> administration of the colony to South Africa. As Mandatory power, South Africa imposed its laws, including racial classifications and rules. From 1948, with the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">National Party</a> elected to power, this included South Africa applying <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> to what was then known as <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a>. </p>
      <p>In the later 20th century, uprisings and demands for political representation by native African political activists seeking independence resulted in the UN assuming direct responsibility over the territory in 1966, but South Africa maintained <i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">de facto</i> rule. In 1973 the UN recognised the South West Africa People's Organisation (<a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a>) as the official representative of the Namibian people; the party is dominated by the Ovambo, who are a large plurality in the territory. Following continued guerrilla warfare, South Africa installed an interim administration in Namibia in 1985. Namibia obtained full independence from South Africa in 1990. However, <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Islands" title="Penguin Islands">Penguin Islands</a> remained under South African control until 1994. </p>
      <p>Namibia has a population of 2.6&nbsp;million people and a stable <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a>. Agriculture, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Namibia" title="Tourism in Namibia">tourism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Namibia" title="Mining in Namibia">mining industry</a>&nbsp;– including mining for gem diamonds, <a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining" title="Uranium mining">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining" title="Gold mining">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_mining" title="Silver mining">silver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Base_metal" title="Base metal">base metals</a>&nbsp;– form the basis of its <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Namibia" title="Economy of Namibia">economy</a>, while the manufacturing sector is comparatively small. The large, arid <a href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a> from which the country derived its name has resulted in Namibia being overall one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and territories by population density">least densely populated</a> countries in the world. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

       <ul> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Pre-colonial_period"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Pre-colonial period</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#German_rule"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">German rule</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name of the country is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a>, the oldest desert in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-at1315_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at1315-20">[20]</a></sup> The name <i>Namib</i> itself is of <a href="/wiki/Nama_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nama language">Nama</a> origin and means "vast place". Before its independence in 1990, the area was known first as <a href="/wiki/German_South-West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="German South-West Africa">German South-West Africa</a> (<i>Deutsch-Südwestafrika</i>), then as South-West Africa, reflecting the colonial occupation by the Germans and the South Africans. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Namibia" title="History of Namibia">History of Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Buschmannkinder.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Buschmannkinder.jpg/220px-Buschmannkinder.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Buschmannkinder.jpg/330px-Buschmannkinder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Buschmannkinder.jpg/440px-Buschmannkinder.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4070" data-file-height="2737"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Buschmannkinder.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a> are Namibia's oldest <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Indigenous peoples of Africa">indigenous</a> inhabitants.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The dry lands of Namibia have been inhabited since early times by San, Damara, and Nama. Around the 14th century, immigrating <a href="/wiki/Bantu_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu people">Bantu people</a> began to arrive during the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> from central Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From the late 18th century onward, <a href="/wiki/Oorlam_people" title="Oorlam people">Oorlam people</a> from Cape Colony crossed the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a> and moved into the area that today is southern Namibia.<sup id="cite_ref-KDA_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KDA-22">[22]</a></sup> Their encounters with the nomadic Nama tribes were largely peaceful. They received the missionaries accompanying the Oorlam very well,<sup id="cite_ref-Dierks_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dierks-23">[23]</a></sup> granting them the right to use waterholes and grazing against an annual payment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVedder1997177_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVedder1997177-24">[24]</a></sup> On their way further north, however, the Oorlam encountered clans of the <a href="/wiki/OvaHerero_people" class="mw-redirect" title="OvaHerero people">OvaHerero</a> at Windhoek, <a href="/wiki/Gobabis" title="Gobabis">Gobabis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Okahandja" title="Okahandja">Okahandja</a>, who resisted their encroachment. The Nama-Herero War broke out in 1880, with hostilities ebbing only after the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> deployed troops to the contested places and cemented the status quo among the Nama, Oorlam, and Herero.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVedder1997659_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVedder1997659-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Europeans to disembark and explore the region were the Portuguese navigators <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo Cão">Diogo Cão</a> in 1485 <sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>and <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> in 1486, but the Portuguese did not try to claim the area. Like most of interior <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, Namibia was not extensively explored by Europeans until the 19th century. At that time traders and settlers came principally from Germany and Sweden. In the late 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Dorsland_Trek" title="Dorsland Trek">Dorsland Trekkers</a> crossed the area on their way from the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">Transvaal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>. Some of them settled in Namibia instead of continuing their journey. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_rule">German rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/German_South_West_Africa" title="German South West Africa">German South West Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua genocide">Herero and Namaqua genocide</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/220px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/330px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg/440px-Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kirche_denkmal_nam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>German church and monument to colonists in Windhoek, Namibia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia became a German colony in 1884 under <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> to forestall perceived British encroachment and was known as <a href="/wiki/German_South_West_Africa" title="German South West Africa">German South West Africa</a> (<i>Deutsch-Südwestafrika</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Palgrave_Commission" title="Palgrave Commission">Palgrave Commission</a> by the British governor in Cape Town determined that only the natural deep-water harbour of <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> was worth occupying and thus annexed it to the Cape province of British South Africa. </p>
      <p>From 1904 to 1907, the <a href="/wiki/Herero_people" title="Herero people">Herero</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nama_people" title="Nama people">Namaqua</a> <a href="/wiki/Herero_Wars" title="Herero Wars">took up arms</a> against brutal German colonialism. In a calculated punitive action by the German occupiers, government officials ordered extinction of the natives in the <a href="/wiki/Herero_and_Namaqua_genocide" title="Herero and Namaqua genocide">OvaHerero and Namaqua genocide</a>. In what has been called the "first genocide of the 20th century",<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> the Germans systematically killed 10,000 Nama (half the population) and approximately 65,000 Herero (about 80% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Adhikari_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adhikari-30">[30]</a></sup> The survivors, when finally released from detention, were subjected to a policy of dispossession, deportation, forced labour, racial segregation, and discrimination in a system that in many ways anticipated the <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> established by South Africa in 1948. </p>
      <p>Most Africans were confined to so-called native territories, which under South African rule after 1949 were turned into "homelands" (<a href="/wiki/Bantustans" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantustans">Bantustans</a>). Some historians have speculated that the German genocide in Namibia was a model for the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazis</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Madley_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Madley-31">[31]</a></sup> The memory of genocide remains relevant to ethnic identity in independent Namibia and to relations with Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The German government formally apologised for the Namibian genocide in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_African_mandate">South African mandate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South African mandate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>During World War I, South African troops under General <a href="/wiki/Louis_Botha" title="Louis Botha">Louis Botha</a> <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa_campaign" title="South West Africa campaign">occupied the territory</a> and deposed the German colonial administration. The end of the war and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> resulted in South West Africa remaining a possession of South Africa as a <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> until 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-Rajagopal_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajagopal-34">[34]</a></sup> The mandate system was formed as a compromise between those who advocated for an Allied annexation of former German and Turkish territories and a proposition put forward by those who wished to grant them to an international trusteeship until they could govern themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-Rajagopal_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajagopal-34">[34]</a></sup> It permitted the South African government to administer South West Africa until that territory's inhabitants were prepared for political self-determination.<sup id="cite_ref-Louis_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louis-35">[35]</a></sup> South Africa interpreted the mandate as a veiled annexation and made no attempt to prepare South West Africa for future autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-Louis_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louis-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">Conference on International Organization</a> in 1945, the League of Nations was formally superseded by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) and former League mandates by a trusteeship system. Article 77 of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a> stated that UN trusteeship "shall apply...to territories now held under mandate"; furthermore, it would "be a matter of subsequent agreement as to which territories in the foregoing territories will be brought under the trusteeship system and under what terms".<sup id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-36">[36]</a></sup> The UN requested all former League of Nations mandates be surrendered to its <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">Trusteeship Council</a> in anticipation of their independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-36">[36]</a></sup> South Africa declined to do so and instead requested permission from the UN to formally annexe South West Africa, for which it received considerable criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-36">[36]</a></sup> When the UN General Assembly rejected this proposal, South Africa dismissed its opinion and began solidifying control of the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Vandenbosch_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vandenbosch-36">[36]</a></sup> The UN Generally Assembly and Security Council responded by referring the issue to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> (ICJ), which held a number of discussions on the legality of South African rule between 1949 and 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-First_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/220px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/330px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg/440px-Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2084" data-file-height="1586"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_homelands_78.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map depicting the Police Zone (in tan) and tribal homelands (in red) as they existed in 1978. Self-governing tribal homelands appear as tan with red stripes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Namibia.jpg/220px-Namibia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Namibia.jpg/330px-Namibia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/Namibia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="374" data-file-height="285"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Foreign Observer identification badge issued during the 1989 Namibian election
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa began imposing <i><a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>,</i> its codified system of racial segregation and discrimination, on South West Africa during the late 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford1-38">[38]</a></sup> Black South West Africans were subject to <a href="/wiki/Pass_laws" title="Pass laws">pass laws</a>, curfews, and a host of draconian residential regulations that heavily restricted their movement. Development was concentrated in the region of the country immediately adjacent to South Africa, formally called the "Police Zone", where most of the German colonial era settlements and mines were. Outside the Police Zone, indigenous peoples were restricted to theoretically self-governing <a href="/wiki/Bantustan" title="Bantustan">tribal homelands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Devils_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devils-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the late 1950s and early 1960s, pressure for global decolonisation and national self-determination began mounting on the African continent; these factors had a radical impact on South West African nationalism. Early nationalist organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/South_West_African_National_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="South West African National Union">South West African National Union</a> (SWANU) and <a href="/wiki/South_West_African_People%27s_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="South West African People's Organisation">South West African People's Organisation</a> (SWAPO) made determined attempts to establish indigenous political structures for an independent South West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Müller_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Müller-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1966, following the ICJ's controversial ruling that it had no legal standing to consider the question of South African rule, SWAPO launched an armed insurgency that escalated into part of a wider regional conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Border_War" title="South African Border War">South African Border War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Caprivi_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caprivi-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As SWAPO's insurgency intensified, South Africa's case for annexation in the international community continued to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-Dobell_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dobell-42">[42]</a></sup> The UN declared that South Africa had failed in its obligations to ensure the moral and material well-being of South West Africa's indigenous inhabitants and had thus disavowed its own mandate.<sup id="cite_ref-Yusuf_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-43">[43]</a></sup> On 12 June 1968, the UN General Assembly adopted a resolution proclaiming that, in accordance with the desires of its people, South West Africa be renamed <i>Namibia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yusuf_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_269" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 269">United Nations Security Council Resolution 269</a>, adopted in August 1969, declared South Africa's continued occupation of Namibia illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-Yusuf_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yusuf-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MAA_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAA-44">[44]</a></sup> In recognition of this landmark decision, SWAPO's armed wing was renamed the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_of_Namibia" title="People's Liberation Army of Namibia">People's Liberation Army of Namibia</a> (PLAN).<sup id="cite_ref-Camp_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Camp-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Namibia became one of several flashpoints for <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> proxy conflicts in southern Africa during the latter years of the PLAN insurgency.<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes-46">[46]</a></sup> The insurgents sought out weapons and sent recruits to the Soviet Union for military training.<sup id="cite_ref-Betram_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Betram-47">[47]</a></sup> SWAPO's political leadership, dependent on military aid from the Soviets, Cuba, and Angola, positioned the movement within the socialist bloc by 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Dreyer_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dreyer-48">[48]</a></sup> This practical alliance reinforced the prevailing perspective of SWAPO as a Soviet proxy, which dominated Cold War ideology in South Africa and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Devils_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Devils-39">[39]</a></sup> For its part, the Soviet Union supported SWAPO partly because it viewed South Africa as a regional Western ally.<sup id="cite_ref-Shultz_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shultz-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SADF-Operations_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/220px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/330px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SADF-Operations_4.jpg/440px-SADF-Operations_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="485"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SADF-Operations_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>South African troops patrol the border region for PLAN insurgents, 1980s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Growing war weariness and the reduction of tensions between the superpowers compelled South Africa, Angola, and Cuba to accede to the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Accord_(Angola)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripartite Accord (Angola)">Tripartite Accord</a>, under pressure from both the Soviet Union and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-SACP_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SACP-50">[50]</a></sup> South Africa accepted Namibian independence in exchange for Cuban military withdrawal from the region and an Angolan commitment to cease all aid to PLAN.<sup id="cite_ref-James_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James-51">[51]</a></sup> PLAN and South Africa adopted an informal ceasefire in August 1988, and a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transition_Assistance_Group" title="United Nations Transition Assistance Group">United Nations Transition Assistance Group</a> (UNTAG) was formed to monitor the Namibian peace process and supervise the return of refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-Sitkowski_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sitkowski-52">[52]</a></sup> The ceasefire was broken after PLAN made a final incursion into the territory, possibly as a result of misunderstanding UNTAG's directives, in March 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-Clairborne_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clairborne-53">[53]</a></sup> A new ceasefire was later imposed with the condition that the insurgents were to be confined to their external bases in Angola until they could be disarmed and demobilised by UNTAG.<sup id="cite_ref-Sitkowski_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sitkowski-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Demob_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demob-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the end of the 11-month transition period, the last South African troops had been withdrawn from Namibia, all political prisoners granted amnesty, racially discriminatory legislation repealed, and 42,000 Namibian refugees returned to their homes. Just over 97% of eligible voters participated in the country's first <a href="/wiki/Namibian_parliamentary_election,_1989" class="mw-redirect" title="Namibian parliamentary election, 1989">parliamentary elections</a> held under a <a href="/wiki/Universal_franchise" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal franchise">universal franchise</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1989_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-55">[55]</a></sup> The United Nations plan included oversight by <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">foreign election observers</a> in an effort to ensure a <a href="/wiki/Election#Difficulties_with_elections" title="Election">free and fair election</a>. SWAPO won a plurality of seats in the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Constituent_Assembly_of_Namibia" title="Members of the Constituent Assembly of Namibia">Constituent Assembly</a> with 57% of the popular vote.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1989_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-55">[55]</a></sup> This gave the party 41 seats, but not a two-thirds majority, which would have enabled it to draft the constitution on its own.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1989_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1989-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Namibian Constitution was adopted in February 1990. It incorporated protection for human rights and compensation for state expropriations of private property, and established an independent judiciary, legislature, and an executive presidency (the constituent assembly became the national assembly). The country officially became independent on 21 March 1990. <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nujoma" title="Sam Nujoma">Sam Nujoma</a> was sworn in as the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Namibia" title="President of Namibia">President of Namibia</a> at a ceremony attended by <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a> of South Africa (who had been released from prison the previous month) and representatives from 147 countries, including 20 heads of state.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1994, following the first multiracial elections in South Africa, that country ceded <a href="/wiki/Walvis_Bay" title="Walvis Bay">Walvis Bay</a> to Namibia.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_independence">After independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: After independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Since independence Namibia has completed the transition from white minority apartheid rule to parliamentary democracy. <a href="/wiki/Multiparty_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiparty democracy">Multiparty democracy</a> was introduced and has been maintained, with local, regional and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Namibia" title="Elections in Namibia">national elections</a> held regularly. Several registered political parties are active and represented in the National Assembly, although the <a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a> has won every election since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The transition from the 15-year rule of President <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nujoma" title="Sam Nujoma">Nujoma</a> to his successor <a href="/wiki/Hifikepunye_Pohamba" title="Hifikepunye Pohamba">Hifikepunye Pohamba</a> in 2005 went smoothly.<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since independence, the Namibian government has promoted a policy of national reconciliation. It issued an amnesty for those who fought on either side during the liberation war. The civil war in Angola spilled over and adversely affected Namibians living in the north of the country. In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Namibia_Defence_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Namibia Defence Force">Namibia Defence Force</a> (NDF) troops were sent to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC) contingent. </p>
      <p>In 1999, the national government quashed a secessionist attempt in the northeastern <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IRIN_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-59">[59]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_conflict" title="Caprivi conflict">Caprivi conflict</a> was initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Liberation_Army" title="Caprivi Liberation Army">Caprivi Liberation Army</a> (CLA), a <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebel</a> group led by <a href="/wiki/Mishake_Muyongo" title="Mishake Muyongo">Mishake Muyongo</a>. It wanted the Caprivi Strip to secede and form its own society. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Namibia" title="Geography of Namibia">Geography of Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namib_Desert_Namibia(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/220px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/330px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg/440px-Namib_Desert_Namibia%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namib_Desert_Namibia(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sand dunes in the <a href="/wiki/Namib" title="Namib">Namib</a>, Namibia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/290px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/435px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg/580px-Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1015" data-file-height="914"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Natural_Earth_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Shaded relief map of Namibia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1376" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_NAM_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Namibia map of Köppen climate classification zones
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 825,615&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (318,772&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Namibia is the world's thirty-fourth largest country (after Venezuela). It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_south" title="17th parallel south">17°</a> and <a href="/wiki/29th_parallel_south" title="29th parallel south">29°S</a> (a small area is north of 17°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_east" title="11th meridian east">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/26th_meridian_east" title="26th meridian east">26°E</a>. </p>
      <p>Being situated between the <a href="/wiki/Namib" title="Namib">Namib</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari</a> deserts, Namibia has the least rainfall of any country in sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Namibian landscape consists generally of five geographical areas, each with characteristic <a href="/wiki/Abiotic_component" title="Abiotic component">abiotic conditions</a> and vegetation, with some variation within and overlap between them: the Central Plateau, the Namib, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">Great Escarpment</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>. </p>
      <p>The Central Plateau runs from north to south, bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">Skeleton Coast</a> to the northwest, the Namib Desert and its coastal plains to the southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a> to the south, and the Kalahari Desert to the east. The Central Plateau is home to the highest point in Namibia at <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigstein,_Namibia" class="mw-redirect" title="Königstein, Namibia">Königstein</a> elevation 2,606 metres (8,550&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-elevation_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elevation-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Namib is a broad expanse of hyper-arid gravel plains and dunes that stretches along Namibia's entire coastline. It varies between 100&nbsp;km (60 miles) and 200&nbsp;km (120 miles) in width. Areas within the Namib include the Skeleton Coast and the <a href="/wiki/Kaokoveld" title="Kaokoveld">Kaokoveld</a> in the north and the extensive Namib Sand Sea along the central coast.<sup id="cite_ref-at1315_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at1315-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Great Escarpment swiftly rises to over 2,000 metres (7,000&nbsp;ft). Average temperatures and temperature ranges increase further inland from the cold <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> waters, while the lingering coastal fogs slowly diminish. Although the area is rocky with poorly developed soils, it is significantly more productive than the Namib Desert. As summer winds are forced over the Escarpment, moisture is extracted as precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Bushveld is found in north-eastern Namibia along the Angolan border and in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>. The area receives a significantly greater amount of precipitation than the rest of the country, averaging around 400&nbsp;mm (16&nbsp;in) per year. The area is generally flat and the soils sandy, limiting their ability to retain water and support agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-Cowling,_S._2001_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowling,_S._2001-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>, an arid region that extends into South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, is one of Namibia's well-known geographical features. The Kalahari, while popularly known as a desert, has a variety of localised environments, including some verdant and technically non-desert areas. The <a href="/wiki/Succulent_Karoo" title="Succulent Karoo">Succulent Karoo</a> is home to over 5,000 species of plants, nearly half of them <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>; approximately 10 percent of the world's <a href="/wiki/Succulents" class="mw-redirect" title="Succulents">succulents</a> are found in the Karoo.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The reason behind this high productivity and endemism may be the relatively stable nature of precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Namibia's Coastal Desert is one of the oldest deserts in the world. Its sand dunes, created by the strong onshore winds, are the highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Because of the location of the shoreline, at the point where the Atlantic's cold water reaches Africa's hot climate, often extremely dense fog forms along the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Near the coast there are areas where the dune-hummocks are vegetated.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Namibia has rich coastal and marine resources that remain largely unexplored.<sup id="cite_ref-Sparks_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sparks-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/220px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/330px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg/440px-SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="822" data-file-height="614"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-cactus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fish_River_Canyon" title="Fish River Canyon">Fish River Canyon</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia-1113.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/220px-Namibia-1113.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/330px-Namibia-1113.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Namibia-1113.jpg/440px-Namibia-1113.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia-1113.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Namibia is primarily a large desert and semi-desert plateau.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia extends from 17°S to 25°S latitude: climatically the range of the sub-Tropical High Pressure Belt. Its overall climate description is arid, descending from the Sub-Humid [mean rain above 500&nbsp;mm (20&nbsp;in)] through Semi-Arid [between 300 and 500&nbsp;mm (12 and 20&nbsp;in)] (embracing most of the waterless Kalahari) and Arid [from 150 to 300&nbsp;mm (6 to 12&nbsp;in)] (these three regions are inland from the western <a href="/wiki/Great_Escarpment,_Southern_Africa" title="Great Escarpment, Southern Africa">escarpment</a>) to the Hyper-Arid coastal plain [less than 100&nbsp;mm (4&nbsp;in)]. Temperature maxima are limited by the overall elevation of the entire region: only in the far south, <a href="/wiki/Warmbad,_Namibia" title="Warmbad, Namibia">Warmbad</a> for instance, are maxima above 40&nbsp;°C (100&nbsp;°F) recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Typically the sub-Tropical High Pressure Belt, with frequent clear skies, provides more than 300 days of sunshine per year. It is situated at the southern edge of the tropics; the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a> cuts the country about in half. The winter (June&nbsp;– August) is generally dry. Both rainy seasons occur in summer: the small rainy season between September and November, the big one between February and April.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Humidity is low, and average <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rainfall</a> varies from almost zero in the <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_Coast" title="Skeleton Coast">coastal desert</a> to more than 600&nbsp;mm (24&nbsp;in) in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a>. Rainfall is highly variable, and droughts are common.<sup id="cite_ref-EBClimate_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-73">[73]</a></sup> In the summer of 2006/07 the rainfall was recorded far below the annual average.<sup id="cite_ref-Olszewski1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olszewski1-74">[74]</a></sup> In May 2019, Namibia declared a state of emergency in response to the drought,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> and extended it by additional 6 months in October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Weather and climate in the coastal area are dominated by the cold, north-flowing <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Current" title="Benguela Current">Benguela Current</a> of the Atlantic Ocean, which accounts for very low <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> (50&nbsp;mm (2&nbsp;in) per year or less), frequent dense fog, and overall lower temperatures than in the rest of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-EBClimate_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-73">[73]</a></sup> In Winter, occasionally a condition known as <i><i lang="de" title="German-language text"><a href="/wiki/Bergwind" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergwind">Bergwind</a></i></i> (German for "mountain breeze") or <i><i lang="af" title="Afrikaans-language text">Oosweer</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> for "east weather") occurs, a hot dry wind blowing from the inland to the coast. As the area behind the coast is a desert, these winds can develop into sand storms, leaving sand deposits in the Atlantic Ocean that are visible on satellite images.<sup id="cite_ref-Olszewski2_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olszewski2-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Central Plateau and Kalahari areas have wide <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal</a> temperature ranges of up to 30&nbsp;°C (86&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-EBClimate_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBClimate-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><i>Efundja</i>, the annual seasonal flooding of the northern parts of the country, often causes not only damage to infrastructure but loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The rains that cause these floods originate in Angola, flow into Namibia's <a href="/wiki/Cuvelai-Etosha_Basin" title="Cuvelai-Etosha Basin">Cuvelai-Etosha Basin</a>, and fill the <i>oshanas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Oshiwambo" class="mw-redirect" title="Oshiwambo">Oshiwambo</a>: flood plains) there. The worst floods so far<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> occurred in March 2011 and displaced 21,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_sources">Water sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Water sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Namibia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Namibia">Water supply and sanitation in Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia is the driest country in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> and depends largely on groundwater. With an average rainfall of about 350&nbsp;mm (14&nbsp;in) per annum, the highest rainfall occurs in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi</a> in the northeast (about 600&nbsp;mm (24&nbsp;in) per annum) and decreases in a westerly and southwesterly direction to as little as 50&nbsp;mm (2&nbsp;in) and less per annum at the coast. The only perennial rivers are found on the national borders with <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, and the short border with <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi</a>. In the interior of the country, surface water is available only in the summer months when rivers are in flood after exceptional rainfalls. Otherwise, surface water is restricted to a few large storage dams retaining and damming up these seasonal floods and their run-off. Where people do not live near perennial rivers or make use of the storage dams, they are dependent on groundwater. Even isolated communities and those economic activities located far from good surface water sources, such as mining, agriculture, and tourism, can be supplied from groundwater over nearly 80% of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>More than 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Borehole" title="Borehole">boreholes</a> have been drilled in Namibia over the past century. One third of these boreholes have been drilled dry.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifer</a> called Ohangwena II, on both sides of the Angola-Namibia border, was discovered in 2012. It has been estimated to be capable of supplying a population of 800,000 people in the North for 400 years, at the current (2018) rate of consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-aqui_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aqui-82">[82]</a></sup> Experts estimate that Namibia has 7,720&nbsp;km<sup>3</sup> (1,850&nbsp;cu&nbsp;mi) of underground water.<sup id="cite_ref-afr_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afr-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aqmap_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aqmap-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies">Communal Wildlife Conservancies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Communal Wildlife Conservancies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/280px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/420px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg/560px-SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SAC_Namibia-bushveld.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Quivertree Forest, <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communal_Wildlife_Conservancies_in_Namibia" title="Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia">Communal Wildlife Conservancies in Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia is one of few countries in the world to specifically address <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_conservation" title="Wildlife conservation">conservation</a> and protection of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a> in its constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-Stefanova_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stefanova-85">[85]</a></sup> Article 95 states, "The State shall actively promote and maintain the welfare of the people by adopting international policies aimed at the following: maintenance of <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecosystems</a>, essential ecological processes, and biological diversity of Namibia, and utilisation of living natural resources on a sustainable basis for the benefit of all Namibians, both present and future."<sup id="cite_ref-Stefanova_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stefanova-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1993, Namibia's newly formed government received funding from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> (USAID) through its Living in a Finite Environment (LIFE) Project.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The Ministry of Environment and Tourism, with financial support from organisations such as USAID, <a href="/wiki/Endangered_Wildlife_Trust" title="Endangered Wildlife Trust">Endangered Wildlife Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, and Canadian Ambassador's Fund, together form a Community Based Natural Resource Management (CBNRM) support structure. The project's main goal is to promote sustainable natural resource management by giving local communities rights to wildlife management and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-UNEP_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/220px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/330px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg/440px-Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="533"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tintenpalast-Windhoek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <center>
          <a href="/wiki/Tintenpalast" title="Tintenpalast">Tintenpalast</a>, the centre of Namibia's government
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Namibia" title="Politics of Namibia">Politics of Namibia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Namibia" title="Elections in Namibia">Elections in Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Draft_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draft-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dual_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dual-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Namibia" title="President of Namibia">President of Namibia</a> is elected to a five-year term and is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CN_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CN-88">[88]</a></sup> All members of the government are individually and collectively responsible to the legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECN_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECN-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Namibia" title="Constitution of Namibia">Constitution of Namibia</a> outlines the following as the organs of the country's government:<sup id="cite_ref-Bösl_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bösl-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Executive: executive power is exercised by the President and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Namibia" title="Cabinet of Namibia">Government</a>.</li> 
       <li>Legislature: Namibia has a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Namibia" title="Parliament of Namibia">Parliament</a> with the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Namibia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Namibia">National Assembly</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Namibia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Council of Namibia">National Council</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parliament153_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament153-92">[92]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a>: Namibia has a system of courts that interpret and apply the law in the name of the state.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>While the constitution envisaged a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> for Namibia's government, the <a href="/wiki/SWAPO" title="SWAPO">SWAPO</a> party has been <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant</a> since independence in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Namibia" title="Foreign relations of Namibia">Foreign relations of Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia has a largely independent <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a>, with persisting affiliations with states that aided the independence struggle, including <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. With a small army and a fragile economy, the Namibian government's principal foreign policy concern is developing strengthened ties within the Southern African region. A dynamic member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, Namibia is a vocal advocate for greater regional integration. It became the 160th member of the UN on 23 April 1990. On its independence it became the 50th member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Namibian_Defence_Force" title="Namibian Defence Force">Namibian Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In early 2020, The Global Firepower Index (GFP) reported that Namibia's <a href="/wiki/Namibia/Military" class="mw-redirect" title="Namibia/Military">military</a> is ranked as one of the weakest in the world, at 126th out of 137 countries. Among 34 African countries, Namibia is also poorly ranked at the 28th position.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Despite this, government spending for the Ministry of Defence stood at N$5,885 million (a 1.2% decrease from the previous financial year).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> With close to 6 million Namibian dollars, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Namibia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Namibia)">Ministry of Defence</a> receives the fourth highest amount of money from Government per ministry. </p>
      <p>Namibia does not have any enemies in <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">the region</a>, though it has been involved in various disputes regarding borders and construction plans.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Namibian <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Namibia" title="Constitution of Namibia">constitution</a> defines the role of the military as "<i>defending the territory and national interests.</i>" Namibia formed the <a href="/wiki/Namibian_Defence_Force" title="Namibian Defence Force">Namibian Defence Force</a> (NDF), comprising former enemies in a 23-year bush war: the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_of_Namibia" title="People's Liberation Army of Namibia">People's Liberation Army of Namibia</a> (PLAN) and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Africa" title="South West Africa">South West African</a> <i>Territorial Force</i> (<a href="/wiki/SWATF" class="mw-redirect" title="SWATF">SWATF</a>). The British formulated the plan for integrating these forces and began training the NDF, which consists of a small headquarters and five battalions. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Assistance_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Transitional Assistance Group">United Nations Transitional Assistance Group</a> (UNTAG)'s Kenyan infantry battalion remained in Namibia for three months after independence to help train the NDF and to stabilise the north. According to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Namibia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Namibia)">Namibian Defence Ministry</a>, enlistments of both men and women will number no more than 7,500. </p>
      <p>The chief of the Namibian Defence Force is Air Vice Marshal <a href="/wiki/Martin_Pinehas" title="Martin Pinehas">Martin Kambulu Pinehas</a> (with effect from 1 April 2020). </p>
      <p>In 2017, Namibia signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg/340px-Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg.png" decoding="async" width="340" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg/510px-Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg/680px-Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="675"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Namibia_14_regions-numbered.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Namibia" title="Regions of Namibia">Regions of Namibia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Namibia" title="Administrative divisions of Namibia">Administrative divisions of Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Namibia is divided into 14 regions which are subdivided into 121 constituencies. The administrative division of Namibia is tabled by <i>Delimitation Commissions</i> and accepted or declined by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Namibia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Namibia">National Assembly</a>. Since state foundation four Delimitation Commissions have delivered their work, the last one in 2013 under the chairmanship of Judge Alfred Siboleka.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Regional councillors are directly elected through secret ballots (regional elections) by the inhabitants of their constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Local authorities in Namibia can be in the form of municipalities (either Part 1 or Part 2 municipalities), town councils or villages.<sup id="cite_ref-alan_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alan-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:left;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Namibia" title="Human rights in Namibia">Human rights in Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Namibia" title="LGBT rights in Namibia">Homosexual acts are illegal in Namibia</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and discrimination, as well as intolerance, against <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Namibia" title="LGBT rights in Namibia">LGBT people</a> is still widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> However, LGBT Namibians face virtually no violence or harassment from the Namibian police, military or government<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and no LGBT Namibians have ever been arrested or charged with sodomy in the last 20–25 years.<sup id="cite_ref-humandignitytrust.org_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humandignitytrust.org-104">[104]</a></sup> Some Namibian government officials and high-profile figures, such as Namibia's Ombudsman John Walters and First Lady <a href="/wiki/Monica_Geingos" title="Monica Geingos">Monica Geingos</a>, have called for sodomy and homosexuality to be decriminalised and are in favour of <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT rights">LGBT rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-humandignitytrust.org_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humandignitytrust.org-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2018, it was reported that 32% of women aged 15–49 have experienced <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Domestic_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic abuse">domestic abuse</a> from their spouses/partners and 29.5% of men believe that physical abuse towards their wife/partner is acceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> On the other hand, the Namibian constitution guarantees the rights, freedoms and equal treatment of women in Namibia<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and SWAPO, the ruling party in Namibia, has adopted a “zebra system”, which ensures a fair balance of both genders in government and equal representation of women in the Namibian government.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Namibia is considered one of the most free and democratic countries in Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> with a government that maintains and protects basic human rights and freedoms. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Namibia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Namibia" title="Economy of Namibia">Economy of Namibia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/220px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/330px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg/440px-Downtown_Windhoek%2C_Independence_Avenue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Windhoek,_Independence_Avenue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Downtown <a href="/wiki/Windhoek" title="Windhoek">Windhoek</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/220px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/330px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG/440px-Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tsumeb-Main_Road.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tsumeb" title="Tsumeb">Tsumeb</a>'s main road
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oyster_farming,_Walvis_Bay_(Namibia).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg/220px-Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg/330px-Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg/440px-Oyster_farming%2C_Walvis_Bay_%28Namibia%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4678" data-file-height="3042"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oyster_farming,_Walvis_Bay_(Namibia).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
